Aa2f words over 3 letters of lengths 15796 and 25379, and a special case of length 1928

A word (or string) is called aa2f (almost abelian square-free) if it does not contain an abelian square uv as a factor - with the exception that the shortest squares of period 1 (|u| = |v| = 1) are allowed. In other words, the repetitions xx and xxx, where x is a letter, are allowed to appear but all the other abelian squares should be avoided.

Originally, the aa2f problem on three letters was posed by Sami Mäkelä in his M.Sc. Thesis, Patterns in words (in Finnish), University of Turku, 2002.
The problem whether there is an infinite word avoiding abelian squares of period more than 1 over the ternary alphabet is still open.
However, a partial solution to this problem was given by M. Rao and M. Rosenfeld in 2015 in their paper "On Mäkelä’s Conjectures: deciding if a morphic word avoids long abelian-powers".
Indeed, they show that abelian squares of period more than 5 are avoidable on the ternary alphabet.
See also their fascinating article from 2016: Avoidability of long k-abelian repetitions, Mathematics of Computation, http://dx.doi.org/10.1090/mcom/3085.

Below, long aa2f words over 3 letters are represented.

The first word is of length 15796 and it was found with the aid of a parallelized JavaScript program written by Alexandr Gavrilenko in 2015.

The following twelve words, each of length 13796, are obtained by taking the middle part of the first word, that is, cutting away the first 1000 and the last 1000 characters, and listing, in alphabetical order, all the six permutations and their mirror images regarding this middle part.

Later, in 2017, a longer aa2f word over 3 letters was computed. The length of this word is 25379 and it was found with the aid of a parallelized Rust program written also by Alexandr Gavrilenko.

The permutations and mirror images of the last word, all of which have a length of 1928, contain no pure repetitions of the form xx, i.e., factors of the form yxxz, where x, y, z are letters and y ≠ x, z ≠ x. As in the case of the aa2f15796 word, the original aa2f1928 word was discovered using a parallelized JavaScript program written by Alexandr Gavrilenko in 2015.

An aa2f word over 3 letters of length 15796 

© 2017 V. Keränen

aa2f15796
